< user_name>
Gregory Wright< /user_name>
< Time>
1584981465676</Time>
< rating>
1< /rating>
< text>
Saying this has been one of the roughest times in my life is an understatement. As most of you know, my beautiful 18 year old daughter died this past week as a result of an automobile accident.

Alaina's accident was on March 17th.
Her car was towed from the scene by LJs towing company, 2600 North Ave Sacramento CA 95838.
At 7am on Wednesday morning, while sitting at my daughter's bedside, I reached out to my friend, Stacey, at Golden State Towing and asked them to get Alaina's car. I don't know why it was important to me to have possession of the car, but I wanted to. I needed to know we had it, and be able to get anything out of it that may be important to the family. I also know we would be being charged a storage fee until the vehicle was picked up.
Stacey immediately contacted LJs and explained my situation. LJs stonewalled her and informed her that can only deal with the registered owner of the vehicle (me). She again explained my daughter was in the hospital on life support and I had given her permission to obtain the vehicle. LJs refused to help. They told Stacey I would have to provide a notarized letter giving her permission to get the vehicle. I told Stacey we would just have to deal with it at a later time, I had more important things to devote my time to.
I heard due to the severity of the crash I, as her mother, should not see the vehicle. And I don't want to. But I wanted Golden State to have it and I wanted my friend to go through the car and get Alaina's personal possessions for me.
Early Saturday morning my daughter was taken into the OR, gifted her organs for donations, and was declared. On Saturday afternoon, my sister had a mobile notary meet at her home to get the letter Stacey needed to obtain my daughter's vehicle.
After Golden State obtained my notirized letter and went to LJs, Stacey faced many issues at the tow yard. They refused to even deal with Stacey, even with the notarized letter. They would not allow Golden State to remove the vehicle or view it because they did not have a printout of their motor carrier permit but had provided a digital copy. LJs proceeded to argue with them about the law delaying the removal process even further. After over an hour, Stacey was finally able to get my baby's car.

LJs has an obvious conflict of interest for towing cars, both on CHP and Sheriff rotation, as they own multiple wrecking yards that profit tremendously for the cars they keep with no intent on releasing. They make the price to obtain your towed vehicle as high as possible in the hopes you cannot afford to retrieve it and make the releasing of the vehicle as unpleasant as possible in hopes you walk away from the car and it can be sent to their own dismantelers to make even more money.

I was charged over $600 for the tow to the yard. They took two trucks out to tow one car, a blatant scam and ploy to obtain more revenue for the tow. $60 a day for storage, and $115 for being there on a Saturday. 5 days, over $1000, less than 10 miles from the site.

What LJs did may have been legal, but it was by no means ethical or moral.

No compassion and horrible buisness dealing.

#crooks</text>

On behalf of Andrea Joy:
Saying this has been one of the roughest times in my life is an understatement. As most of you know, my beautiful 18 year old daughter died this past week as a result of an automobile accident.

Alaina's accident was on March 17th.
Her car was towed from the scene by LJs towing company, 2600 North Ave Sacramento CA 95838.
At 7am on Wednesday morning, while sitting at my daughter's bedside, I reached out to my friend, Stacey, at Golden State Towing and asked them to get Alaina's car. I don't know why it was important to me to have possession of the car, but I wanted to. I needed to know we had it, and be able to get anything out of it that may be important to the family. I also know we would be being charged a storage fee until the vehicle was picked up.
Stacey immediately contacted LJs and explained my situation. LJs stonewalled her and informed her that can only deal with the registered owner of the vehicle (me). She again explained my daughter was in the hospital on life support and I had given her permission to obtain the vehicle. LJs refused to help. They told Stacey I would have to provide a notarized letter giving her permission to get the vehicle. I told Stacey we would just have to deal with it at a later time, I had more important things to devote my time to.
I heard due to the severity of the crash I, as her mother, should not see the vehicle. And I don't want to. But I wanted Golden State to have it and I wanted my friend to go through the car and get Alaina's personal possessions for me.
Early Saturday morning my daughter was taken into the OR, gifted her organs for donations, and was declared. On Saturday afternoon, my sister had a mobile notary meet at her home to get the letter Stacey needed to obtain my daughter's vehicle.
After Golden State obtained my notirized letter and went to LJs, Stacey faced many issues at the tow yard. They refused to even deal with Stacey, even with the notarized letter. They would not allow Golden State to remove the vehicle or view it because they did not have a printout of their motor carrier permit but had provided a digital copy. LJs proceeded to argue with them about the law delaying the removal process even further. After over an hour, Stacey was finally able to get my baby's car.

LJs has an obvious conflict of interest for towing cars, both on CHP and Sheriff rotation, as they own multiple wrecking yards that profit tremendously for the cars they keep with no intent on releasing. They make the price to obtain your towed vehicle as high as possible in the hopes you cannot afford to retrieve it and make the releasing of the vehicle as unpleasant as possible in hopes you walk away from the car and it can be sent to their own dismantelers to make even more money.

I was charged over $600 for the tow to the yard. They took two trucks out to tow one car, a blatant scam and ploy to obtain more revenue for the tow. $60 a day for storage, and $115 for being there on a Saturday.  5 days, over $1000, less than 10 miles from the site.

What LJs did may have been legal, but it was by no means ethical or moral.

No compassion and horrible buisness dealing.

#crooks</review>

<Review>The Airstream Orange County Service Department and Personnel are incompetent and irresponsible.

Since taking ownership of our brand-new Interstate about 4 months ago, our van has been in the Service department on and off for over 6 weeks. In October, I brought the van in to deal with a few minor problems and a Mercedes recall which should have been dealt with prior to delivery. When I picked it up two weeks later, there was a dent and deep scratches on the front fender that cannot be just polished away. Airstream service blamed Mercedes but took no responsibility. Around November, one of the CZone monitors and the Fantastic fan malfunctioned. It took them over 3 weeks to get parts and another week to have them installed. They blamed COVID-19 for the delays and it finally got fixed this past weekend 3 months later. Around December, we started to get a chassis battery low voltage warning. I brought the van in last week and they determined that the battery minder settings needed to be changed and said they fixed it. Last night, while boondocking for a single night with my wife, we got the same warning message; obviously, not fixed. When I picked up the van this past Saturday, I had questions regarding the Victron Solar Management system. Their Tech told me all solar power goes to the House batteries, which is incorrect as one of the panels is dedicated to the chassis battery. The tech angrily insisted he was correct because in his own words ‚ÄúI‚Äôve installed solar panels on million-dollar homes‚Äù. That may be so, but he doesn‚Äôt know much about the solar power system on a 2020 Interstate.

I rarely give bad reviews. I am 55 years old and have better things to do. Having owned numerous cars and boats in my lifetime, I expected to have problems with what can be considered a small condo on wheels. The one-star review is not really about the issues outlined above. It is mostly about feeling violated from what I saw (and smelled) when picking up my van this past Saturday. I brought the van in for service last week with empty waste tanks. I picked it up this past Saturday with the black tank at 45%. Apparently, their techs were using my van as their own personal toilet. Not only did they fail to dump their own waste from the tank prior to pick up, they didn‚Äôt even have the decency to clean the toilet bowl, which looked like it was violated by a pack of Parvo infected dogs.
I texted a complaint to my salesperson yesterday, who immediately notified the operations manager who contacted me today to offer cheap remorse. He was pleasant enough on the phone and apologetic but once again, assumed no responsibility. He stated that none of his staff members admitted to using our toilet (what a surprise) and then goes on to tell me they have a homeless problem in the area and suggests that perhaps the van was left unlocked and used by a homeless person. If this is the case, the operations manager at a minimum is admitting to mismanagement, and at worst, gross incompetence.  Leaving our van unlocked at night while being aware of a local homeless problem is even more problematic than a dirty toilet bowl.

If you are local to Orange County and buying a new Airstream because you hope not to drive too far when service is needed (as we did), you may want to think twice. Yes, they are beautiful rigs, well designed and engineered, but like all other RV‚Äôs are prone to problems. This is a very nice place to see a good selection of Airstream trailers. They have short trailers about 16 feet long to 27 feet long, lots of color choices inside the trailers and even have the new Nest trailer. The one made of three pieces of fiberglass on the outside of the trailer.

<userid>103340259159603573407</userid><name>Bob Vreeland</name><Time>1529982281244<//Time>< rating>
5< /rating>
< text>
First and foremost, this place is a barber shop. It is not a Sport Clips or Supercuts, not a salon, not a spa. It is a barber shop. There are no reservations or appointments, you get your chair after everyone else who was there before you. The last cut is 15 minutes before the listed close time, so don't be late!  Payments are CASH ONLY. They do have an ATM in the corner of the shop, but you should still have cash on hand before walking in as a courtesy to the barbers.  The cut pricing is reasonable. $20 for an adult cut, $5 for a beard trim, $16 for a child cut, and $14 for military (with a valid ID).

The barbers are professionals. Let them know what you're looking to get done and they will make it happen. If you don't have an idea as to what you want, figure it out before you sit down. Help them help you!

Some rebuttals for those who have expressed concerns:
- Yes, even though it is busy and there is a line, they are allowed to take breaks to go and get food or to make a Starbucks run. As mentioned before, if you do not want to wait in line, don't. Nobody is forcing you to be here. Go make an appointment at one of the franchised hair salons and they will help you out. If you feel like the barbers have no sense of urgency, that's on you. Leave. Again, nobody is forcing you to be here.
- If you can find a cheaper haircut elsewhere, go for it. Again, nobody is forcing you to be here. A 1 star rating because you don't want to pay $20 for a haircut makes you look bad (which is probably the case if you're paying $8 for a haircut from WalMart).<//text>

< Review>
I reallyyyyyyy REALLY wanted to like this place since it's only two blocks from where I work and the food is decent. However, the last couple of times I've gone there, I've had issues. I once ordered spring rolls that cost me almost $10 to only be disappointed by the unauthentic taste and shortage of portion. I basically got two small chubby wrapped spring rolls, with coleslaw veges and fresh-out-of-the-pan hot tofu pieces.

The last time I went, I ordered their Mushroom eggplant basil dish, with chicken. When receiving my order, I noticed that the portion was a tad bit on the short side but assumed it was because of the huge bowl it was served in. After a couple of bites, I couldn't find any mushrooms or bell peppers. I let the cashier know and apparently, they were out. Why would you serve the item when you don't have all of the ingredients, and sell it for the same price of almost $10? Ridiculous. He told me he'll comp me the next time I go back, but how is he going to keep track of that? Humph!< /Review>

< Review>
Great little affordable eatery when you want a quick bite (very limited counter seating inside & just a couple tables outside). All prices include tax (yes!) and are generally around $8 for what seems to be more-authentic-than-most Thai food.

The curry I tried wasn't marked spicy but definitely had some spice kick, so be sure to ask first if you're spice sensitive. My friend is addicted to their Pad See Ew.

FYI: They are closed 3-5PM, so don't show up then! Heard they may start being open on weekends (hurray!)< /Review>

< Text>
I'm a teacher and I just spent 10hrs packing up my classroom for the summer. Being exhausted from packing and needing a storage space ASAP, I was not looking forward to the task of sifting through all the google search results. Finally I decided to just call Public Storage and see what their "$1 first month deal" was really all about. There has to be a catch, right?

I was so wrong. Darryl picked up their central helpline and was professional, friendly, and incredibly helpful. He even found a better deal closer to me. On top of that he's a veteran! If you need help Darryl is your man. Hands down.

The same day, I went to this location and the manager, Felicia, was just as helpful. I was running a bit late due to traffic and she stayed during her lunch break to meet with me. The process was simple and easy. Next thing I knew, I was moving my things in and I was done.

In summary, based on my interactions with Darryl and Felicia, Public Storage is quick, easy, clean, and friendly. I will definitely come here again and recommend this facility.< /Text>

Never again. I travel 75% of the year. My first impression was underwhelming but hopeful. DO NOT stay in the main lodge. The hallways are DARK, and the smell is reminiscent of a sewer! I am NOT exaggerating. We immediately requested an upgrade and as a VIP Gold member we are offered an upgrade if available. While a Villa was available they refused to offer it UNLESS we paid an extra $120, over the approximately $500 paid. Additionally, plan to pay a resort fee and parking that will run you about $100 total. The Villas are much nicer but are in SERIOUS need of a remodel and updating. I could go on and on and on but you get the drift. GO SOMEPLACE ELSE!!!!!!< /review>

<Rating>5< /Rating>< text>
A jewel in the hills of Hollywood.
There are some hotels that feel alive and tell a story to the guest lucky enough to stay; This is one of those hotels. A journey back into a time when things were fun, a feeling of moving forward and immediately present is displayed upon entering this sleek unpretentious hidden hotel. The professional staff from valet, doorman, reception and housekeeping that always greet you w/a sincere smile - never saccharine.  It's an older hotel that has kept itself clean and polished over the years and has updated itself appropriately, and tastefully. The lush gardens are beautiful and beckon you to stroll before or after a lovely dinner at Cavatina. A wondefully romantic restaurant w/a well thought out wine list.
The cuisine prepared by Luis Morales is fresh, bright and bursting w/subtle nuances and the staff in the restaurant are more than accommodating. There is a levity that is pervasive on the grounds w/an abundance of rock and roll photography and paraphernalia.  This hotel might be in the heart of Hollywood but feels like an oasis w/twinkling fairy lights and a calm hush over a private retreat. The two pools are clean, cool and deep....I'm six foot two inches and despise these kiddie pools so many hotels favor presently. The large absorbent towels provided at poolside is a major plus and a detail often overlooked by many. The limited poolside menu  had options for all types of appetites. My family and I look forward to our return soon. Thank you to the entire staff at the Sunset Marquis, sorry this review is 6 months old but the heartfelt feelings are still on point. A special thanks to Yoman for providing such wonderful hospitality.< /text>

<resp>None< /resp>< review>
My wife and I spent five nights at Sunset Marquis and we really enjoyed our stay. The hotel room was large, with a really comfy bed and amazing walk in shower. Our room also had a large adjoining balcony, which was useful for afternoon drinks, overlooking the pool, and the occasional afternoon siesta.
We stayed from Monday to Saturday, so the atmosphere at the pool was pretty quiet during the week days and nights, however I assume, based on the Friday night and Saturday morning, that the atmosphere is a lot better on the weekend - perhaps making one's stay even more fun.
There was a slight problem upon check-out, where the valet charged us for three nights, rather than the actual one. (I wonder if this was intentional, to see if we wouldn't notice). However, this was rectified immediately.
The front counter staff were terrific. Our flight out of LA was not til midnight, and checkout was at midday. They took our bags and kept them securely, allowing us to explore the city for the next several hours, and come back and chill by the pool until it was time to go to the airport.
I'd definitely recommend this hotel to couples of families looking to have a fun and relaxing time in West Hollywood. The hotel is beautiful, and the room is comfortable. It is a bit on the pricey side, but hey - it's Hollywood!</review>

< rate>
5</rate>
< Review>
A very tranquil quiet zen place in the heart of Sunset Strip. You will be whisked away by several things: the beautiful green landscaping, the black and white photographs of the legends of music and acting who have dined or stayed there and the serenity and quiet.

There are numerous comfortable sitting areas throughout the hotel, as well as benches placed in garden areas. It was wonderful to be able to sit and enjoy the beauty of it all, and close my eyes to hear the trickling fountains - without the noise of traffic or other city distractions.

The restaurant, Cavatina, is an indoor outdoor dining establishment. Be sure to check out the photo at the entrance of the restroom - I found it quite humorous :-) Food and service excellent. There is a lounge by the pool and and the entrance (Bar 1200), as well as a small cocktail area at the restaurant. And, there is a spa!

This hotel is not located on main road of this area. It is at the end of cul de sac surrounded by several luxury apartment houses, accordingly a "hidden gem". There is a rich history here; the hotel has undergone a number of changes since 1970s party days, and some of the history is evident by their "wall of fame"! Be sure to check out Morrison Gallery, which has rotating exhibits on various musicians.

I look forward to my next visit! Excellent service, I felt like a VIP from moment I entered to the time I left - worth every dime for the tranquil zen feeling!< /Review>

<user_id>108597451951810892807</user_id>< username>
Bower Louber</username>
<Time>1371667868327<//Time>< Rating>
5< /Rating>
< Review>
I went over to the Sunset Marquis last night to catch up with some old friends that where in town for a few days from Florida. My friend was very excited that she got her picture taken with Steven Tyler the night before and she told me that I would love the place.

I was on my motorcycle so I didnt have to deal with the valet parking / lack of street parking fiasco that all car drivers have to deal with so I cruised right up and parked up front. I found my friends in the back at the restaurant bar and they started to take me for a tour.

This is a high end rock n roll hotel through and through. There is a recording studio on the facility called NightBird Recording Studios. Some heavy stuff has gone down here at the studios and here are a few artists that have recorded here.

Aerosmith
Billy Idol
Dave Navarro
Elton John
Gene Simmons
George Clinton
Heart
Madonna
Phil Collins
Ozzy Osbourne ... and that is just a few of the names.

I walked around and checked out both of the pools and checked out some of the nice villas. This place is really high end and is within walking distance of the Sunset strip. Very Cool!

We had a few cocktails at the bar downstairs and they played tons of old 70s rock which was awesome and it was loud! The place reaked of Nag Champa which was also a nice touch.</Review>
